<user_id>117203263979676497714<//user_id>< Review>
Incredible experience with Sierra Nevada Tire in Pollock Pines!

So last September, I took my truck in for an oil change and had them check the brakes. They asked me if there was anything wrong and I told them no, just that I've had the truck 10 years, driven 65,000 miles and have yet to replace the brakes. I get my truck after service and they say the brakes are fine. Probably 30-40% left, but still OK. I was pretty pleased that they didn't decide to just tell me I need new brakes and charge me ... I would have said fine and never known any different.

Now today, I had brought my little Honda Fit in because I heard some light grinding when the car was rolling - this was without the braked being used. I thought uh-oh I must be close to metal and metal and better get the brakes done before I've got to replace the rotors too (been there, done that in years past). So i get a call this morning from them telling me my brakes are fine, not need to replace them - but they did notice my tires needed to be rotated and did so. OK - i was fine with that. Also - again thinking they could have just replaced the brakes and charged me and I would have been happy.

So here's the kicker: When I sign the receipt - it says $0. I question the fellow - and he says "...brake inspections are free..." I then say, "but you rotated the tires...". He said - "well, I had them off anyway....just come see us when you need new tires...". You're damn right I will! In fact, that's where I'm taking both vehicles for all service. WOW - an HONEST car service place!!!! Had I gone to a dealership they would have charged me through the nose and probably found more things to "repair" and charge me for.

What an incredible experience. Sierra Nevada Tire gets all my business for now on! Thank you!!!</Review>

<Gmap_id>0x809ac752521dd4b7:0xed6203e6786bc36d<//Gmap_id><name>Bill A< /name><Review>I do not usually write reviews, but my experience with California Moss Control  warrants an exception.

I needed someone to clean the gutters on my two-story home so I entered my contact info into the Home Advisor search engine.  Chris (who I later learned was the owner of Cal.  Moss Control) called me within minutes to schedule an appt for an estimate.

I really didn't understand why a "gutter cleaning" company was called "moss control," but when Chris gave me the estimate he also schooled me on the corrosive effects of the green moss that was growing in my relatively new roof.  It was a form of black mold that feeds on the lye in the composite shingles and that spills off the roof and covers the sidewalk and driveway.  I always thought the green slime we dealt with during the winter was attributed to the northward orientation of our house--not so.  It was digesting my roof and the lye in my aggregate driveway.

So I agreed to hire Chris to clean my gutters, treat my roof and to power wash my sidewalks and driveway.

I cannot overstate how professional and expert he and his crew were.  They treated my property as though it was their own.  And they are environmentally friendly:  Instead of washing everything down the street gutter they opened my sewer and channeled all the effluent into the city sewers.

Yes, I paid for more than a simple gutter cleaning, but every time I walk out front or drive into my driveway I think of how thankful I am for the education Chris gave me.  He saved my expensive roof and ridded me of the green moss I had resigned to live with.  I will definitely use California Moss Control again and will recommend the company highly to all my family and friends!  Thank you Chris!!!!<//Review>< Rating>

<userid>108649344011016756337< /userid><username>Jeffrey Ho< /username><date>1616817109962</date><Rate>5< /Rate>< Review>
Indoor dining tonight 3/26/2021. This a Japanese owned ramen restaurant. I had their black garlic tonkotsu ramen $15, geso (squid) fry $7, red rice beer $5, yuki white peach $5. Having ate over hundreds of bowls of ramen throughout my years in Japan, I can tell their ramen is authentic. The flavors are fantastic and when I closed my eyes, it brought back memories of when I ate at ramen parlors in Tokyo. This place is better though as I was the only person dining indoors. There's no rush feeling you get when there's a line outside waiting. Here are the reasons why I absolutely love their ramen:

- å‘³ä»˜ã‘çŽ‰å­ ramen egg soft boiled and is marinated. Perfect jelly on the inside
- broth is heavy and have been cooked for hours
- great garlic flavor
- perfectly soft chashu
- fresh noodles

My bill was $42 with tax and tip. Service here was excellent. Great job everyone at Waraku, especially the chef. My dinner was perfect.< /Review>

< text>
Tuesday night dinner for 3. Appetizers (goyza and edamame) and drinks came out alarmingly fast. Meals followed after a reasonable lag to enjoy first courses. Waters were always filled. Staff was very attentive. Broth was good quality, temperature was okay. If you like really hot broth I would mention it while ordering. Extra noodles came out on the side. The meats were not traditional cutting style but nevertheless were great. If you don't want a 100% traditional bowl this place is great.< /text>

< Text>
The best Tonkotsu ramen in JTown by far. Broth is rich and creamy. Wonderful on a cold, winter day in The City. Reasonably priced for what you get. Love their warm, gooey smoked egg in the hot broth. Pressing your own fresh garlic cloves is a novel idea. Never had that experience before. You do have to ask for a garlic press though. The best deal on the menu is to order the Kakuni Don instead of the Small Bites size for your table to share - you get Waraku's heavenly tasting braised pork belly, but also rice and more gooey egg. Also enjoyed their hot black tea, different from the usual watery green tea you get a Japanese restaurant these days. Service was ok, nothing memorable or outstanding (hence the 4 stars).<//Text>

<review>It was already 9pm and we wanted to eat some ramen~ We ended up in japantown after trying to go to another ramen shop and seeing a huge line... decided we didn't have the time and headed here because there are many many ramen places here. The only one we knew was already closed so we came to waraku because of the food reviews and because it was still pretty to, good sign, i thought.

We got the tonkotsu ramen ($10.99) with extra noodles on the side ($2), and a mini kakuni rice bowl ($4). The bowls look smaller than the regular one, But the quality is good, and I think quantity is enough too. There just probably won't be many leftovers to bring home. The ramen came with an egg, some thin pieces of meat, a mushroom type, ginger.. and the broth was less salty than average, which was good~~
The rice bowl had just 1 piece of meat, But it was a very big piece. The meat was very tasty, also sweet, and the rice was impregnated with the sauce, very yummy. Btw we ordered all without spring onions, but othrewise you'd have that too.
Service was quite attentive, some of the servers are Japanese and some others are not , But they're certainly trained to look japanese.
Good experience, would repeat<//review>< Pictures>

I was rather disappointed by Waraku. From the rather bland decor to unenthusiastic service to lackluster ramen.

I had their tsukemen, which is supposed to be a much heavier, richer broth than standard tonkatsu. Unfortunately, that wasnâ€™t the case at Waraku where the tsukemen was thin, and with exception of a heap of scallions, relatively light on flavor. Noodles were a bit unusual, coming with some kind of oil and seasoning on them. Temperature is a huge part of ramen, and Waraku fell short there, too, serving the tsukemen broth too hot which prevents it from sticking to the noodles, and serving an overcooked ajitama egg at refrigerated temperatures.

Drink options left much to be desired. There werenâ€™t many great pairings with the food, and even the sake menu seemed content to put middling options on a pedestal.

One positive note: the chicken karaage, while far from traditional, was really delicious. I ordered the plate with rice, but I think the wait staff misheard me and I wound up with the protein-heavy version sans rice, but no complaints.</Text>

<text>I had the spicy tonkotsu ramen, tako wasabi, and some karage at Waraku. The tako wasabi was pretty straightforward and good; plenty of wasabi and prepared well.
The karage came with a lemon wedge and some mayo based sauce to dip in. The seasoning was pretty light, but the breading was very crispy. Enjoyed it very much.
The ramen was decently spicy, noodles were pretty straightforward, not made in house. The broth was a bit light on flavor, which was slightly masked by the spicyness. They add cilantro to some of the ramen, which is a little odd, but not bad. The ajitamago (seasoned boiled egg) was well seasoned, but a bit more well done than I prefer. Overall, I enjoyed it. Not quite as good as Yamadaya or Marufuku, but nowhere near the wait time, sometimes convenience trumps all.< /text><pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipN8IXxQdMTrxmTknxO4Nbu-kXpnF7oj9paznkPD=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]<//pics><Response>None</Response>< Gmap_id>

< text>
Very good ramen.

I devoured my chicken one quickly. My wife had the spicy one and she loved it.

The chicken karage is the best we've ever had.  Boneless, tender, perfectly fried (not oily).  Our son is a picky eater and he said it was the best chicken he's ever had.

They also have a pork belly rice dish which is perfect for non ramen fans and very reasonably priced.

A great casual option in Japan town.  Reviews said it fills up fast with wait times but we got in without a wait on a week night.<//text>

<user_name>SubUrbanSF< /user_name><Time>1530572139298</Time>< rating>

< Review>
My youngest son turned me on to Waraku.
Told me it was "different" from our regular "ramen joint". We were first in at opening. The young lady that served us was very soft spoken so it was a lil difficult to understand her but her friendliness and level of "cuteness" made up for that.
Now listen... this is "different".
Their ramen is made with a "bone broth" that I imagine is cultivated the same as sourdough bread (Google the process)
It was DELICIOUS!
So delicious that I went in strictly as a spectator as my son was hungry and I was not...
I tasted his ramen (this is very telling as he is not one to share but it was so good and different from the norm that he WANTED me to taste it)...
I tasted his ramen and was so turned on by the bone broth flavor, I ordered one for myself purely for flavor and not for hunger.
Here's where it gets tricky...
One of the great challenges for any restaurant is consistency.
I failed to mention the ramen has a roasted garlic component. On My sons dish... it was PERFECT!
I guess they rushed mine as the garlic was just over the burn line. Instead of roasted, my garlic was burned. As much as I tried to muscle thru it as I didn't want a refire and really wanted to have the bone broth win the flavor battle... the burned garlic won. Shoulda sent it back. Ate half and took it home.
A lil water and soy sauce fixed it right up!
Meanwhile, their "MACHA FLAN (?)"?!
THA BOMB!!ðŸ˜². NOT TOO "MACHAY" DIDN'T TASE LIKE I WAS EATING GRASS WHICH WAS MY FEAR WHEN I ORDERED IT. really, it rocked. Overall, something special here at WARAKU!!
Definitely going to give them a second try and would suggest it to anyone that asked.
That's why I took the time for this. That and hopefully the owners/cooks see this and balance the garlic roast a lil better cause if it wasn't for the overpowering effect of the burnt garlic... this would 5+ stars!
Give WARAKU a try.
Enjoy!

<Review>Waraku used to be my absolute favorite ramen place in the city.  But lately I have been finding their fare inconsistent at best.  Don't get me wrong, it is still better than most.  The smoked eggs have come out practically hard boiled the last few times, rather than the runny yolk that everybody wants.  They also seem to be very affected by how busy they are.  Best case, go here on a "school night" when restaurants are supposed to be slow.  The broth will be much better than average, the noodles with that great QQ taste, and if you happen in on a good night, 3/4 of the meat will be great.  If it's a Friday or Saturday night, save yourself the time and go get a burrito or something.< /Review>< date>

< review>
The wait for a 4 person table took a while, and the place was pretty loud. However, the ramen was good. I had the tonkotsu. The broth is really good and the noodles are cooked just right. The pork is a bit sweet and fatty for my liking. The smoked egg is pretty interesting. They forgot to add the sweet corn I ordered, but they brought out a small dish when I mentioned it. We shared a few other dishes as well: seaweed salad, agedashi tofu and spicy noodle spring rolls. None of the appetizers were as good as the ramen.</review>

<rating>5< /rating>< text>
Well y'all.
I've found my favorite ramen in the Bay (for now).

The ramen is AMAZE but their other food items were also all REALLY good which I didn't expect of a ramen-specific place.

Worth the wait (if there is one). Get the tonkotsu ramen, $9 - the broth is rich and borderline creamy, even. The mouthfeel and taste is a must-try and the noodles are perfect. Comes with fresh garlic - ask for a garlic press!

We also tried:
Sashimi salad - which is HUGE for $9 and totally a steal
Tako (octopus) wasabi & ika shio kara (salted squid), $3 each - portion was small but so fresh -- interesting and concentrated flavors
Agedashi tofu $5 - HOLY - yes plz
Takoyaki $4.5 - ON POINT

DEFINITELY RETURNING AND RECOMMENDING.
Oh yes, the interior is beautiful and upscale. But I'm hurr to eat.</text>

<Text>I came here for lunch with my girlfriend and cousin and ordered the Deluxe Tonkotsu Ramen. This ramen place is probably my favorite in San Francisco right now because of all the ingredients they put into the ramen, the service, and the decorations in the restaurant. The noodles were delicious and had a nice chew to them. The broth was very flavorful and rich. We also asked for garlic and they gave us a garlic press.I liked how you could press your own fresh garlic cloves. The chashu was tender but the pork belly wasn't as good as the chashu. I liked that this ramen came with corn because my girlfriend's favorite food is corn and probably made this place one of our favorites. The egg was runny just the way I like it but everyone else at my table had an overcooked egg. Sucks for them =P. I'll probably come back often to eat the Deluxe Tonkotsu Ramen.</Text>< Pics>

<Rate>3<//Rate><review>Came here for lunch during the J-pop festival. It was a really nice and well decorated place. Service was good and fast.

I had the deluxe tonkotsu ramen with the spicy miso paste (not spicy at all). The broth was very savory and flavorful. The pork was soft and tender. The EGG had tons of flavor which was a good surprise. Overall pretttttttttttty good ramen. I'd give it 4 stars but I feel they messed up on one of the key components - the noodles. My noodles were under cooked and were too chewy for my liking. The portions were also too small for the price. 13$ and I was hungry 10 minutes after eating. I feel like noodles are cheap, just throw a bunch in there to fill us up.

I'd come back again to give it another shot, especially cause there aren't too many great ramen places in the city (or have yet to find).

Must haves:

< Text>
New favorite ramen place in SF! I still can't compare it to Ramen Dojo in San Mateo, but i still love this place!

There's garlic cloves on the table, and if there isn't a garlic press on table, ASK FOR ONE! About one clove of garlic really enhances the flavor of the ramen.

I wasn't a huge fan of the tsukemen but it seems to be a popular item on the menu.

Dinner menu has a few extra things on it compared to the lunch menu.  Chicken karaage, gyoza, and kobe beef are delicious too.<//Text>
